<div id="review_1607957890" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1607957890" />
    <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli"><img alt="Pearl Angeli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588420465p2/31514572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1607957890?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=bad-boys">bad-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=mind-blown">mind-blown</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=cute-book-couple">cute-book-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=fangirling">fangirling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=highly-recommended-na">highly-recommended-na</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=sobfest">sobfest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=owned-physical-copy">owned-physical-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1607957890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17292589698925680996">(Buddyreading this book with my lovely sis <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10731189-eunice-moral' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eunice</a>)<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"When love strikes someone like lightning, so powerful and intense it can't be denied. It's beautiful and messy, cracking a chest open and spilling their soul out for the world to see. It turns a person inside out, and there's no going back from it."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391493742ra/8398761.gif' width='350' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>A <b>5/5 Sempre Stars</b> for this book!<br/><br/><br/><b>I believe this is one of the best books written so far.</b> <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18338465.Sempre__Forever___1_' title='Sempre (Forever, #1) by J.M. Darhower' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sempre</a> is yet another masterpiece where <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5351355.J_M__Darhower' title='J.M. Darhower' rel='nofollow noopener'>J.M. Darhower</a> uses a dark theme as a plot device for a YA/N</span>
  <span id="freeText17292589698925680996" style="display:none">(Buddyreading this book with my lovely sis <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10731189-eunice-moral" rel="nofollow noopener">Eunice</a>)<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"When love strikes someone like lightning, so powerful and intense it can't be denied. It's beautiful and messy, cracking a chest open and spilling their soul out for the world to see. It turns a person inside out, and there's no going back from it."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391493742ra/8398761.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A <b>5/5 Sempre Stars</b> for this book!<br><br><br><b>I believe this is one of the best books written so far.</b> <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18338465.Sempre__Forever___1_" title="Sempre (Forever, #1) by J.M. Darhower" rel="nofollow noopener">Sempre</a> is yet another masterpiece where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5351355.J_M__Darhower" title="J.M. Darhower" rel="nofollow noopener">J.M. Darhower</a> uses a dark theme as a plot device for a YA/NA romantic genre. <br><br>The story centered around <b>Haven</b> who grew up as a slave under the Antonelli family. She was about to escape and ask for help when she stumbled upon <b>Dr. Vincent DeMarco</b> who brought her to his home and basically gave her shelter. In return, she was also to work as his slave-- with restrictions and certain rules to never get out of the house or open any code inside. In her new home she met the notorious bad boy <b>Carmin DeMarco</b>, a <i>Mafia prince</i> who has the entire world under his fingertips. What soon blossomed between them was an unexpected love which eventually became a complication to their situation where danger continues to threaten them and heavy decisions matter.<br><br>I loved the concept of this book and the exquisite romance of two young people who fell in love against seemingly impossible odds. I expected it to be something different, something that I'm used to in a Mafia romance, but I was surprised by its uniqueness. The writing of J.M. Darhower and the ardent tone she used gave me a plethora of different emotions.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>She was quiet, running her fingers across his abs and tracing his scars with her fingertips. "How about we just be Haven and Carmine? We don't know the ending, but we can always hope for the best."<br><br>"I like that," he said. "Besides, there's a reason we don't know how a story ends."<br><br>"Why?"<br><br>"Because it doesn't."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Carmine and Haven's love story was one of a kind. I absolutely loved their exchange of lines and the way their cheesy yet heart-warming conversations moved me. It also helped a lot that Carmine was such a cocky, sarcastic, yet very passionate and sweet guy. Just a heads up, this guy is extremely jealous and possessive but I admit to myself that I didn't have any problem with him being that way because well, who am I to complain? His character was defined so perfectly and I just could't do anything but SWOON.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You were brought to me for a reason, for us to save each other. Because you weren't the only one needing to be saved, Haven. I was drowning, and you rescued me."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>At first I did have a little problem with the <b>pacing</b>. The book, I admit, did drag out too long. <b>BUT!</b> I realized when I got to Chapters 40 and beyond that those dragging scenes were a necessity. They were like spices that made the whole book entirely meaningful and dramatic. If the story did not finish with a BOOM, and if the story didn't have that beautiful <i>climax</i>, then I'd probably resent its slow-pacing but then I loved how the overall story turned out so it didn't become a problem with me.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>There were many places Carmine would go back to, many things he would have done differently, but one thing he wouldn't take back was what he had done to save her.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>As a whole, this book was a <b>real surprise</b>. The drama, the sentiments, the dilemma, and even the slow-burn flaw that the author managed to convey were so overwhelming and thought-provoking. I cried a lot of times as I went through its pages (How could an author do that to me?) and I experienced a great deal of adrenaline-rush after reading those action scenes in the near-end. It was just so good!!!<br><br>To those who love heavy drama and romance with action-packed scenarios, you definitely should read this book. I cannot be alone in this, guys! I have to get you to read and experience the beauty of this book, too!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Their love existed, despite everything else, and it was the love that would go on forever. The moment was etched in time, transcending the constraints put on them by life..</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><p>
  <a href="https://bibliopearl.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446199662i/16763926._SX540_.jpg" alt="Pearl's Book Journey (1)" width="380" height="190" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</p><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445993261i/16730770.jpg" width="200" height="120" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="17292589698925680996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_457442388" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/457442388" />
    <a title="Aму" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10342872-a"><img alt="Aму" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411959522p2/10342872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/457442388?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aму" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aму" href="/user/show/10342872-a">Aму</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781456527730" href="/book/show/13111733-sempre">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aму by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/5382243-lou">Lou</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10342872-a?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10342872-a?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10342872-a?shelf=kidnapped-or-forced">kidnapped-or-forced</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10342872-a?shelf=highschool-romance">highschool-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer457442388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11963990053522816567">This was the <i>sweetest</i> yet most <i>heartbreaking</i> and <i>gut-wrenching</i> story I have read in such a long time, that I was actually having trouble believing my eyes. It’s almost like the author got a hold of my collection on GR and took bits and pieces from some of my favorite books and brought them together. That is how good it was. So I honestly can't even begin to describe HOW amazing this book was. (But I will try<b>!</b>) Being entirely engrossed in a way that had me still thinking about these characters in</span>
  <span id="freeText11963990053522816567" style="display:none">This was the <i>sweetest</i> yet most <i>heartbreaking</i> and <i>gut-wrenching</i> story I have read in such a long time, that I was actually having trouble believing my eyes. It’s almost like the author got a hold of my collection on GR and took bits and pieces from some of my favorite books and brought them together. That is how good it was. So I honestly can't even begin to describe HOW amazing this book was. (But I will try<b>!</b>) Being entirely engrossed in a way that had me still thinking about these characters in the middle of reading another book... well actually I've since read two books and still had these characters or their story out of my mind.<br /><br /><i>Sempre</i> was an exceptionally written book that tells the story of people who lived beyond the worlds of human-trafficking and the Mafia. It was a story of sacrifice, acceptance, choices and love. Haven and Carmine were two people who grew up in complete opposite worlds but thrown together to find freedom, love and meaning in their life through each other. I had so many conflicted emotions while reading this and at some point I find myself even loving those people who were on the '<i>bad</i>' side. Which just proved how compelling and striking this book was but I was glad that the author remained very realistic when it comes to the outcome of the actions taken in the story. I was also impressed that Darhower was never afraid to kill her characters<b>!</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ *<b>drops to knees</b>* WHY DID SHE TAKE NICHOLAS FROM ME? WHY! *<b>sobs</b>* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Although most of them were just minor but boy, almost all her characters were pretty striking so when they died - it hit you where it hurt<b>!</b><br /><br /><b>Characters</b>:<br /><br /><i>Carmine</i> - He's a tattooed, spoiled, self centered, foul mouthed, self destructive, hot-headed mafia <i>principé</i>. I can't even begin to describe my feelings towards him. At this point, I don't even care that he was a 17 year old when the story began (I USUALLY like my men older than me.) because wow, all I can really come up with is wow. He used girls for one reason, he didn't treat anyone with respect, he was selfish, and he was reckless.. until he met Haven, until he saw something in her that he wanted.. no, he needed. He wanted to get to know her, he wanted to spend time with her, and for once in his life he didn't mind her being around or touching his things. I don't know what it was about Carmine, but I couldn't get enough of him. Watching him interact with Haven was touching.. especially when he would begin to lose his temper and would either try and back track or would stumble through an apology because the last thing he wanted to do was hurt her in any way. All of the Italian endearments that he murmurs to Haven, will melt your heart. Beating up Nicholas every time he gets to close to her, will give you butterflies. And trying to pick out the perfect picnic blanket for his first real date, will warm the soul. He's like a big steamy bowl of Italian soup on a cold winter's day. *<b>happy sigh</b>*<br /><br /><i>Haven</i> - She is patient, loving and encouraging, all things that have been lacking from Carmine's life for so long. There are times when Haven seems really young, and other times she seems more mature. I think this is consistent to her background. My heart broke for her many times over, but I loved watching the self discovery and seeing her grow into herself. Her development and progress in Carmine’s world such as, meeting his friends and learning how to do small things she never dreamed of, like grocery shopping and driving, had me utterly fascinated. She was strong and intelligent in her own way, she may of been innocent when it came to the basic things about life but she had deeper and a greater perspective than anyone else when it came to life and death. I can't even imagine all those things she had to endure (God how I wish her "<i>Masters</i>" would of had a lot more gory of a death..What<b>?</b> They deserved it<b>!</b>) but I was greatly impressed by this girl.<br /><br /><i>Vincent</i> - My, my.. *<b>blushes</b>* That man had to of been a behind closed doors Dom. His constant dominance, protection of what is '<i>his</i>', and tying Haven to the bed<b>?</b> (Yes. I know that was meant to be a punishment..But hey<b>!</b> He could of tied her up just as easily to something else in the bedroom<b>!</b>) Merely those few clues sent off tiny flares that told me there was more to this man than a doctoral degree and a nice ride.<br /><br />Besides the amazing main characters, there are so many other great characters that you learn to love and hate in this book. The author does an amazing job with developing the characters; making you care about them; giving you the necessary background information that helps to explain; and finally she brings several story lines together towards the end that explains, shocks and leaves you wanting more. Good thing there is a second book in the works and from what I hear a movie deal for this book<b>!</b> *<b>hyperventilates</b>* I don’t know what else to say but.. READ THIS BOOK<b>!</b> Now.. I'm serious<b>!</b> Get out of this page and read the book<b>!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11963990053522816567" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer12648287102011138580">That's it! <b>I've had enough!</b><br/><br/>There's so much in here that rubs me the wrong way, I'm surprised I've gone this far as it is.<br/><br/><b> DNF @70%</b><br/><br/><u>I'll start with the worst, and move on upward</u><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404415331ra/10235241.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><b>It was waaaaaay too long and too slow!!!</b> I mean, this is like reading someone's diary: all the meals they're having, bathroom breaks, lectures at school, overstuffed descriptions, constant dialogues that don't contribute to the story - there's only so much your brain needs to get the image. Why overdo it? Quantity doesn't n</span>
  <span id="freeText12648287102011138580" style="display:none">That's it! <b>I've had enough!</b><br><br>There's so much in here that rubs me the wrong way, I'm surprised I've gone this far as it is.<br><br><b> DNF @70%</b><br><br><u>I'll start with the worst, and move on upward</u><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404415331ra/10235241.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><b>It was waaaaaay too long and too slow!!!</b> I mean, this is like reading someone's diary: all the meals they're having, bathroom breaks, lectures at school, overstuffed descriptions, constant dialogues that don't contribute to the story - there's only so much your brain needs to get the image. Why overdo it? Quantity doesn't necessarily mean quality. If I were to edit this book, it will shrink to the one third of it. The rest is absolutely useless, in my opinion. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/73617.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><b>Love at first sight</b> is a guarantee for a boring romance, not to mention a huge mistake in a book of 1500 epub pages. What does it leave a reader with? Exactly - nothing to look forward to. In my case, it also means being unable to connect to the couple and believe in their romantic relationship.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404416407ra/10235368.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><b>Carmine,</b> who is your typical rich and spoilt teenager, behaving like a first-class asshole and a womaniser. Not only is he drinking alcohol more often than not and uses drugs, but he also <b>pushes an innocent girl whom he claims to like do the same!</b> Oh, and don't forget his violence towards anybody who will as much as <i>look</i> at the girl, landing those guys in a hospital! What kind of chivalry is that? And, as soon as the magical L-word is out (which was way sooner than realistically possible), the guy drops all his 'faults' and becomes a saint. Sorry, but I don't buy this kind of <i>romance</i>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404416114ra/10235340.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><b>Absence of steam.</b> None whatsoever. I can handle it better in a normal-sized book, but to go for so long without any adrenaline is stressing me out. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/614776.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><b>Mafia world.</b> It's my personal opinion, of course, but when the mafia is the central force in the story, I can't help but dislike it normally. There are exceptions, but this was not one of them unfortunately. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404416114ra/10235341.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><b>Lack of drama</b>. And by this I mean the lack of anything significant. There was no hardship for two young people to become close, no problems, arguments or even misunderstandings in their relationship. The only captivating thing about the MCs and the whole book in general, was the mysterious past of the girl and what was so important about her role that turned DeMarco's world upside down. This was <b>the only reason </b> I kept on reading. And as soon as my questions were answered more or less, I've decided to give up...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382532374ra/5964551.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Finally, I don't know if I'm getting older, but I found myself much more fascinated with Carmine's father, Vincent. I'd much rather see <i>him</i> recover from his loss, try to redeem himself and stop this lonely existence. If I cared for anybody's happy ending here, it would be his. But for some reason, I don't see it happening, so there goes my last hope.<br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12648287102011138580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9935904888846781170">This was terrible as fanfiction and I'm assuming will be even worse as self pull-to-publish, just by the names.<br/><br/>ETA: Just to clarify, I read about 10 chapters of this when it was fanfiction and couldn't force myself to read on. I was simultaneously offended that the author thought that a slave/owner relationship could be anything but unequal in power structure and bored at the writing style.<br/>The author's website says she has made large edits, which I applaud, and I want to point out that I have no</span>
  <span id="freeText9935904888846781170" style="display:none">This was terrible as fanfiction and I'm assuming will be even worse as self pull-to-publish, just by the names.<br /><br />ETA: Just to clarify, I read about 10 chapters of this when it was fanfiction and couldn't force myself to read on. I was simultaneously offended that the author thought that a slave/owner relationship could be anything but unequal in power structure and bored at the writing style.<br />The author's website says she has made large edits, which I applaud, and I want to point out that I have not actually read this book in its current form. However, I saw enough earlier that unless she started from scratch (unlikely, from the book description), I have ZERO desire to read it. And neither should you.<br /><br />And just a little PSA to everyone: please educate yourself on human trafficking. There are a multitude of resources available to you. And it is NOT SEXY.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tnc9+R8fpAwLH7j9lbeYzNxySJMKEKSXR4ofHLYktJeMUVQrpEFtZKw0DJxiQpITCi2vW8SdKvAc9Fmte2dGDQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qknjvzFcdqL+GYyMmPP08ygIYonzyfQncbt1QXJsCziQb4ptigK/ylkyOO1vBv4s/leFQT1EekAqxTPwvy/5og==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

        $('bookCover_31369570').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_31369570').hasClassName('ignored')) {

              return;

            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});

        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
